Diyat — Blood Money

Definition and Types of Khata' (Accidental Killing)
Defines khata', splits into two types, and discusses definitional refinements

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define khata', differentiate between its two types (error in intention and error in act), and state the ruling (kaffarah and diyah on 'aqilah) with its proof.

Core Idea
Khata' includes both error in intention and error in act; both require kaffarah and diyah on the 'aqilah.

This passage from Bahr al-Raiq defines khata' and unpacks its two subtypes. The author of the matn gives examples, and the commentator clarifies the categories while critiquing overly narrow definitions. Understanding this classification is essential for correctly applying the Quranic ruling on accidental killing.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of khata'
Locate the author's definition in the matn: shooting at a person thought to be game or combatant but turns out Muslim, or shooting at a target and hitting a human, and similar cases.
The definition includes both types.
2
Distinguish the two types
The commentator explains: (1) error in intention (khata' fi al-qasd) – the shooter's intent was wrong (e.g., thought the victim was an enemy); (2) error in act (khata' fi al-fi'l) – the shooter intended a lawful act (e.g., target practice) but accidentally hit a human.
Note the difference: in type 1, the act is accurate but the intention is mistaken; in type 2, the intention is fine but the act goes astray.
3
Examine the critique of definitions
The commentator argues that the matn's examples are only instances, not comprehensive definitions. He cites al-Wiqayah's better formulation and then Sadr al-Shari'ah's definition, which is further criticized by al-Islah wa al-Iydah for omitting cases like a falling object.
This shows the scholarly process of refining legal definitions.
4
Identify the ruling and its proof
The ruling for true khata' is kaffarah (freeing a slave or equivalent) and diyah (blood money) on the 'aqilah. The proof is Quran 4:92 and the consensus (ijma') based on 'Umar's practice.
The 'aqilah are the paternal relatives who pay diyah as a form of social insurance.
5
Apply the definition to the sleeping person case
A sleeping person rolling over and killing someone is treated like khata' by analogy, though not true error, because the act is voluntary (sleeping movement) and liability attaches.
This expands the scope of khata'-like rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (والخطأ وهو أن يرمي شخصاً ظنه صيداً أو حربياً فإذا هو مسلم أو عرضاً فأصاب أدمياً وما جرى بمجراه كالنائم إذا انقلب على رجل فقتله الكفارة والدية على العاقلة والقتل بسبب كحافر البئر وواضع الحجر في غير ملكه الدية على العاقلة) قوله وهو أن يرمي شخصاً إلى آخره تفسير لنفس الخطأ فإنه على نوعين: خطأ في القصد وخطأ في الفعل. وقد تبين النوعين بقوله وهو أن يرمي شخصاً ظنه صيداً أو حربياً فإذا هو مسلم» تفسير للخطأ في القصد لا في الفعل حيث أصاب ما رمى وإنما أخطأ في القصد أي الظن حيث ظن المسلم حربياً والآدمي صيداً. وقوله أو عرضاً فأصاب آدمياً» هذا بيان للخطأ في الفعل دون القصد فيكون معذوراً. أقول : في عبارة الشارح والمصنف هنا تسامح فإنه قال في تفسير الخطأ في القصد وهو أن يرمي شخصاً يظنه صيداً إلى آخره. وقال في تفسير الخطأ في الفعل وهو أن يرمي عرضاً فيصيب آدمياً. ولا يخفى أن كل واحد من نوعي الخطأ . منحصر فيما ذكره في تفسيره بل الذي ذكره في تفسير كل واحد منهما جزء من جزئياته فكان منه جداً فلم يصلح لأن يكون تفسيراً له فكان الظاهر أن يقال في كل واحد منهما وهو غير في أخص نحو أن يرمي إشارة إلى العموم كما تداركه صاحب الوقاية حيث قال : وفي الخطأ قصداً كرميه مسلماً ظنه صيداً أو حربياً وفعلاً كرميه عرضاً فأصاب آدمياً ا.هـ. ثم إن صدر الشريعة قال في شرح الوقاية : الخطأ :ضربان خطأ في القصد وخطأ في الفعل. فالخطأ الذي في الفعل إن يقصد فعلاً فيصدر منه فعل آخر كما إذا رمى الغرض فأخطأ فأصاب غيره هذا . الخطأ هو الفعل. وأما الخطأ في القصد هو . أن لا يكون الخطأ في الفعل وإنما يكون الخطأ. في قصده، فإن قصد بهذا الفعل حربياً لكن أخطأ في ذلك القصد وهو الغرض حيث لم يكن قصده ا هـ. ورد عليه صاحب الإصلاح والإيضاح حيث قال : الخطأ في الفعل أن لا يصدر عنه الفعل الذي قصده بل فعل آخر وليس كذلك فإنه إذا رمى عرض رضاً فأصابه ثم رجع عنه أو تجاوز إلى ما وراءه فأصاب رجلاً يتحقق الخطأ في الفعل والشرط المذكور ههنا مفقود في الصورتين .. ثم إنه من وجه آخر حيث اعتبر القصد فيه وذلك غير لازم فإذا سقط من يده خشبة أو لبنة فقتل رجلاً يتحقق الخطأ في الفعل ولا قصد فيه ا هـ . وقول المؤلف عرض رضاً» هذا معطوف على قيد وظاهره أن الرمي معتبر في الخطأ في الفعل وليس كذلك فإنه لو سقط منه خشبة أو لبنة فقتل رجلاً هذا خطأ في الفعل ولا رمي. وقوله كنائم انقلب على رجل تفسير لما جرى مجرى الخطأ لأن هذا ليس بخطأ حقيقة ولما وجد فعله حقيقة وجب عليه ما أتلفه كفعل الطفل فجعله كاخطأ لأنه محذور كالمخطئ، وإنما كان حكم المخطئ ما ذكره لقوله تعالى فيه فتحرير رقبة مؤمنة ودية مسلمة إلى أهله ﴾ [النساء : ۹۲] وقد قضى به عمر رضي الله تعالى عنه في ثلاث سنين بمحضر من الصحابة من غير نكير فصار إجماعاً . أخطأ
He (the author), may Allah have mercy on him, said: (And error (khata') is that he shoots a person whom he thinks is game or a combatant, then it turns out to be a Muslim; or (shoots) at a target and hits a human; and what is similar to it, like a sleeping person who rolls over onto a man and kills him – (in these cases) kaffarah and diyah on the 'aqilah; and killing by cause, like the digger of a well and the placer of a stone in another's property – the diyah is on the 'aqilah). His saying 'that he shoots a person...' to the end is an explanation of khata' itself, for it is of two types: error in intention and error in act. He has clarified the two types by his saying 'he shoots a person he thinks is game or a combatant, then it turns out to be a Muslim' – this is an explanation of error in intention, not in act, because he hit what he shot at, but he erred in intention, i.e., assumption, thinking the Muslim was a combatant and the human was game. His saying 'or at a target and hit a human' – this is a statement of error in act without intention, so he is excused. I say: In the wording of the commentator and the author here there is looseness; for he said in explaining error in intention: 'that he shoots a person he thinks is game...' etc., and he said in explaining error in act: 'that he shoots at a target and hits a human'. It is not hidden that each of the two types of error is encompassed by what he mentioned in its explanation, but rather what he mentioned in the explanation of each is a part of its particulars, so it was very limited and not suitable as a definition. So the apparent would be to say in each of them something more general, as the author of al-Wiqayah remedied by saying: 'And in error in intention, like his shooting a Muslim he thinks is game or a combatant; and in act, like his shooting at a target and hitting a human.' Then Sadr al-Shari'ah said in Sharh al-Wiqayah: 'Error is of two types: error in intention and error in act. Error in act is that he intends an act but a different act results, as when he shoots at a target and misses and hits another – this is error in act. As for error in intention, it is that there is no error in the act, but the error is in his intention; for he intends this act towards a combatant, but he errs in that intention, and the intention, where it is not his intent.' The author of al-Islah wa al-Iydah objected to him, saying: 'Error in act is that the act he intended does not occur, but another act occurs. That is not so; for if he shoots at a target and hits it, then it rebounds or goes beyond and hits a man, error in act is realized, yet the aforementioned condition is absent in both images. Furthermore, from another perspective, he considered intention in it, but that is not required; if a piece of wood or brick falls from his hand and kills a man, error in act is realized with no intention in it.' And the author's statement 'at a target' is connected to the restriction, and it apparently implies that shooting is considered in error in act, but it is not so; for if a piece of wood or brick falls from him and kills a man, this is error in act with no shooting. And his statement 'like a sleeping person who rolls over onto a man' is an explanation of what runs in the course of error, because this is not truly error; but since his act is truly found, he is liable for what he destroyed, like the act of a child; so he is made like one who errs because he is in a situation like the mistaken. And the ruling of the mistaken is what he mentioned, due to the Almighty's saying (in the verse) 'then the freeing of a believing slave and blood money delivered to his family' [al-Nisa’ 4:92]. And 'Umar, may Allah be pleased with him, decreed it in three years in the presence of the Companions without any objection, so it became consensus. He erred.
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage is a definition and explanation of khata' (accidental killing) from the matn and its commentary. The author defines khata' as shooting at a person thought to be game or a combatant but turns out to be a Muslim, or shooting at a target and hitting a human, and similar cases (like a sleeping person rolling over and killing someone). These require kaffarah (expiation) and diyah (blood money) on the 'aqilah (tribal insurer). The commentator then breaks down the definition: khata' is of two types – error in intention (khata' fi al-qasd) and error in act (khata' fi al-fi'l). The example of shooting at a person thought to be game is error in intention because the shooter intended to kill game but missed the target in intention; the act itself hit what was aimed at. The example of shooting at a target and hitting a human is error in act: the shooter intended to hit the target but accidentally hit a human. The commentator criticizes the author's and the commentator's own expression, stating that the examples given are only particular instances, not comprehensive definitions. He then cites the correction by the author of al-Wiqayah, who defines error in intention as shooting a Muslim thinking him to be game or a combatant, and error in act as shooting at a target and hitting a human. Sadr al-Shari'ah's definition in Sharh al-Wiqayah is presented but then objected to by the author of al-Islah wa al-Iydah, who argues that error in act can occur without the intended act being different; e.g., shooting at a target and hitting it but then the arrow rebounds and hits someone else – that is error in act even though the intended act (hitting the target) occurred. The commentator further notes that the author's mention of 'shooting' in the definition implies that error in act requires shooting, but that is not necessary; a falling brick or wood is also error in act. The sleeping person rolling over is treated like error (even though not true error) because the act is existent, so liability attaches. The ruling of khata' – kaffarah and diyah on the 'aqilah – is supported by the Quranic verse (4:92) and the practice of 'Umar, which became consensus.

Key Terms
الخطأ (al-khata'): Accidental killing: killing that occurs without intent, either by error in intention (e.g., mistaking a Muslim for an enemy) or error in act (e.g., aiming at target but hitting a person).
العاقلة (al-'aqilah): The tribal insurer or group liable for paying diyah in cases of accidental killing; traditionally the paternal relatives.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is an example of khata' fi al-fi'l (error in act) according to the Hanafi school?
A) Shooting at a person thinking he is a deer
B) Throwing a stone at a target and hitting a passerby
C) Intentionally striking a person with a sword
D) Rolling over in sleep and crushing a child

Key Takeaway
Khata' is categorised into error in intention and error in act, both incurring kaffarah and diyah on the 'aqilah, with the Quran and Ijma' as proofs.

Diyat — Blood Money
beginner
6 min
Killing by Cause: Liability of the 'Aqilah
States ruling for killing by cause: diyah on 'aqilah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for killing by cause (qatl bi-sabab) and identify that the diyah is payable by the 'aqilah, not the killer personally.

Core Idea
In killing by cause, the diyah is on the 'aqilah, not the direct perpetrator.

This lesson examines a concise ruling from the matn regarding indirect killing (qatl bi-sabab). The examples of digging a well or placing a stone on another's property illustrate a situation where death results from a hazard created without intent. The Hanafi school categorizes this as accidental killing, shifting the blood money to the 'aqilah (the paternal relatives). Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly assigning liability in homicide cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act
Recognize that the act described (digging a well, placing a stone) is 'killing by cause' – indirect, without direct physical contact.
The act is done on another's property (في غير ملكه), a necessary condition for this ruling.
2
Apply the Hanafi Classification
Classify the killing as accidental (khata') because the intent was not to kill, and the death is attributed to a hazardous setup.
This triggers the rule that diyah is on the 'aqilah, not the individual.
3
State the Ruling
Conclude: 'The diyah is on the 'aqilah.' This means the killer's paternal relatives are collectively responsible for the blood money.
The matn explicitly says 'al-diyah 'ala al-'aqilah'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : ( والقتل بسبب كحافر البئر وواضع الحجر في غير ملكه الدية على العاقلة
He (the author), may Allah have mercy on him, said: (And killing by cause, like the digger of a well and the placer of a stone in another's property – the diyah is on the 'aqilah).
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This is a concise ruling statement from the matn regarding killing by cause (qatl bi-sabab). The examples given are: a person digs a well on another's property without permission, causing someone to fall in and die; or someone places a stone in another's property, causing someone to trip and die. In such cases, the diyah (blood money) is obligatory on the 'aqilah (the tribal insurer or the killer's paternal relatives), not on the killer personally, because the killing is indirect and considered a form of accidental death (khata'). This is consistent with the Hanafi principle that for unintended killings, diyah is on the 'aqilah. The text does not provide further details or proofs, but it is part of the larger discussion of homicide.

Key Terms
القتل بسبب (al-qatl bi-sabab): Killing by cause: death caused indirectly through an action that creates a hazard (e.g., digging a well, placing a stone) without direct physical contact.
العاقلة (al-'aqilah): The 'aqilah: the group of paternal relatives (or insurer) who collectively pay the diyah for unintentional killings.
الدية (al-diyah): Blood money: financial compensation paid to the victim's heirs for homicide or injury.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, who is liable for the diyah in a case where someone places a stone on another's property and a person trips and dies?
A) The person who placed the stone personally
B) The 'aqilah of that person
C) The property owner
D) No one

Key Takeaway
For killing by cause on another's property, diyah is payable by the 'aqilah, not the individual.

Diyat — Blood Money

Ruling on Madman, Child, or Animal Brandishing Weapon
Intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab dispute on diyah for killing a madman/child/animal in self-defense

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on diyah for killing a madman or child in self-defense and explain the reasoning behind the intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab disagreements.

Core Idea
A madman or child lacks intent, so their inviolability remains; defensive killing requires diyah, not qisas.

Imagine a person threatened by a madman wielding a sword. If the threatened person kills the madman in self-defense, is he liable? The Hanafi school says yes: he must pay diyah (blood money). But why not qisas? And what if it is a child or an animal? This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the ruling and the reasoning behind it, addressing disagreements within the Hanafi school and with al-Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core scenario and ruling
The matn states: if a madman brandishes a weapon and the threatened person kills him intentionally, diyah is wajib. This also applies to a child and an animal.
The ruling applies to intentionally killing the aggressor in self-defense.
2
Locate the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Yusuf holds that no diyah is due for a child or madman because their actions are not legally considered, similar to an animal whose injury is hosed (jabar).
Abu Yusuf's view is a minority within the Hanafi school.
3
Analyze the inter-madhhab disagreement
Al-Shafi'i says no compensation at all because the killing is pure defense, analogous to killing a sane adult aggressor.
Al-Shafi'i compares to a slave brandishing a weapon where no guarantee is due.
4
Examine the Hanafi proof (dalil)
The action of the madman/child is not prohibited (not haram), so it does not drop inviolability. Qisas is prevented by the defense permission, so diyah substitutes.
The Hanafi response: lack of correct choice preserves inviolability.
5
Understand the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under the Hanafi position, the killer pays diyah to the heirs (or owner for animal). Under al-Shafi'i, nothing. Under Abu Yusuf, diyah for animal but not for child/madman.
The mufta bihi is the majority Hanafi view: diyah is due for all three.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وإن شهر المجنون على غيره سلاحا فقتله المشهور عليه عمدا تجب الدية) وهذا على الصبي والدابة وعن أبي يوسف رحمه الله تعالى : لا تجب الدية في الصبي والمجنون. وقال الشافعي رحمه الله تعالى : لا يجب الضمان في الكل لأنه قتله دفاعاً فصار كالبالغ العاقل وهذا لأنه يصير محمولاً على قتله بفعله كان قال له اقتلني وإلا قتلتك وكون الدابة مملوكة للغير لا تأثير له في وجوب الضمان كالعبد إذا شهر سيفاً على رجل فقتله فإنه لا يجب الضمان فكذا هذا فصار كالعبد إذا صال على الحر فقتله. ولأبي يوسف إن فعل الصبي والمجنون معتبر أصلاً حتى لا يعتبر في حق وجوب الضمان لأن جناية العجماء جبار وكذا عصمتها لحقها، وعصمة الدابة لحق المالك فكان فعلهما مسقطاً لحقهما لعصمتهما فلا يضمنان ويضمن الدابة بخلاف الصيد إذا صال على المحرم أو صيد الحرم على الحلال لأن الشارع أذن في قتله ولم يوجب علينا تحمل أذاه ألا ترى أن الخمس الفواسق أباح قتلها مطلقاً الأذى منها فما ظنك إذا تحقق الأذى ومالك الدابة لم يأذن فيجب الضمان؟ وكذا عصمة عبد الغير الحق نفسه وفعله محظور فتسقط به عصمته. ولنا أن الفعل من هذه الأشياء غير متصف بالحرمة فلم يقع بغياً فلا تسقط العصمة به لعدم الاختيار الصحيح ولهذا يجب القصاص على الصبي والمجنون بقتلهما، فإذا لم تسقط كان قضيته أن يجب القصاص لأنه قتل معصومة إلا أنه لا يجب القصاص لوجود المبيح وهو دفع الشر فتجب الدية.
He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And if a madman brandishes a weapon against another, and the threatened person kills him intentionally, diyah is obligatory.) And this applies to a child and an animal. And from Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on him: diyah is not obligatory for a child and a madman. And al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, said: No guarantee is obligatory in all cases because he killed him in defense, so he becomes like a sane adult. And this is because he is compelled to kill him by his action, as if he said to him: kill me or I will kill you. And the fact that the animal is owned by another has no effect on the obligation of guarantee, like a slave if he brandishes a sword against a man and he kills him, then guarantee is not obligatory. Likewise this, so it becomes like a slave if he attacks a free man and he kills him. And according to Abu Yusuf, the action of a child and a madman is not considered legally at all, so it is not considered with regard to the obligation of guarantee, because the injury of a dumb animal is hosed (jabar). Similarly, their inviolability ('ismah) is due to themselves, but the inviolability of an animal is due to the owner. So their act does not drop their right, due to their inviolability. So they are not liable, but the owner of the animal is liable. Contrary to game if it attacks a muhrim or game of the Haram attacks a non-muhrim, because the Lawgiver has permitted killing it and has not imposed upon us bearing its harm. Do you not see that the five noxious animals are permitted to be killed absolutely due to their harm? What then if harm is certain, and the owner of the animal has not permitted it? Then guarantee is obligatory. Similarly, the inviolability of a slave owned by another pertains to the right of himself, and his action is prohibited, so his inviolability falls. And our proof: the action of these entities is not characterized by prohibition (hurmah), so it does not constitute rebellion (baghy), so inviolability is not dropped due to lack of correct choice. For this reason, qisas is obligatory on a child and a madman if they kill. So if inviolability is not dropped, the consequence would be that qisas is obligatory because killing a protected person, except that qisas is not obligatory due to the existence of a permissibility (mubih), which is repelling evil, so diyah is obligatory.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage deals with the situation where a madman (majnun), a child (sabi), or an animal (dabbah) brandishes a weapon against someone. The ruling given in the matn is that if the threatened person intentionally kills the madman, diyah (blood money) is obligatory, not qisas. This also applies to a child and an animal. There are two opposing views: Abu Yusuf holds that no diyah is obligatory for a child or a madman because their actions are not legally considered, similar to an animal whose injury is hosed (jabar). Al-Shafi'i holds that no compensation is due at all because the killing is in defense, analogous to a sane adult; he compares it to a slave who brandishes a weapon and is killed with no liability. The Hanafi position (Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad) is that diyah is due. Their reasoning: the actions of these beings are not prohibited (not haram), so they are not rebellious (baghi), and their inviolability ('ismah) is not dropped because they lack sound choice. However, qisas is not applicable because there is a legal permission (ibahah) to repel evil, so diyah is imposed instead. Additionally, they argue that for a child or madman, qisas would normally be obligatory if they kill someone, but here the permission to defend prevents qisas, leaving diyah. For an animal, the owner is liable because the animal's inviolability is tied to the owner's property right. The disagreement with Abu Yusuf is an intra-Hanafi dispute, while al-Shafi'i's view is an inter-madhhab difference.

Key Terms
المجنون (al-majnun): A person who is insane; lacking legal capacity (ahliyyah) but still possessing inviolability ('ismah).
دية (diyah): Blood money, a financial compensation paid to the heirs of a person who is killed unlawfully but without intent.
عصمة ('ismah): Inviolability; the protected status of a person's life and property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what is the ruling if a madman brandishes a weapon and someone kills him in self-defense?
A) No liability, because the madman's action justified his death.
B) Qisas is obligatory on the killer.
C) Diyah is obligatory on the killer.
D) The killer must pay compensation to the madman's estate for the weapon.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the inviolability of a child or insane person is not lost by their aggressive actions, so killing in self-defense requires diyah, not qisas.

Qisas and Diya for Hand and Foot Amputations
Diya and qisas for amputations of hands, feet, and fingers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which qisas is applicable for hand/foot amputations and identify when diya or hukumat al-adl substitutes.

Core Idea
Qisas requires exact similarity; when impossible, diya or hukumat al-adl applies.

This lesson examines the Hanafi rulings on qisas (retaliation) and diya (financial compensation) for amputations of hands, feet, and fingers. The central principle is that qisas is only valid when the limb is standard and perfectly equivalent; otherwise, compensation is determined by fixed diya or equitable assessment (hukumat al-adl). We will explore the conditions, exceptions, and payment rules as derived from classical Hanafi sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
What is the act under discussion? Amputation of a hand or foot. The default ruling is that if done intentionally and without right, it incurs either qisas or diya depending on conditions.
The act is not defined as a specific crime but as a cause for liability.
2
State the general principle of similarity (mumathala)
Qisas requires precise similarity between the injury inflicted and the retaliation. For hands and feet, this means same limb, same side, same location (e.g., from the wrist/ankle). The text says similarity is considered except when the cut is from the glans (likely meaning the joint).
Mumathala is a condition for qisas.
3
Analyze exceptions to similarity
When the cut is not at the root (e.g., partial cut), or when the limb is not standard (supernumerary finger, already missing/paralyzed hand), similarity is impossible, so qisas is not applicable. Instead, diya or hukumat al-adl applies.
Intra-Hanafi differences exist on what constitutes 'root' (Abu Yusuf vs. Abu Hanifa).
4
Determine the compensation type
If the cut is of a standard hand/foot from the joint, full diya (fixed amount) is due. If the cut is above the shoulder or foot (i.e., beyond the limb), hukumat al-adl (judge's assessment) applies. For supernumerary or already missing limbs, hukumat al-adl applies.
Diya for a hand is payable in two-year installments.
5
Note special cases (slave, partial cuts)
Breaking a slave's hand/foot does not trigger immediate compensation. The text also mentions that for aqta' (missing hand) or ashal (paralyzed), there is no qisas if the remaining hand is cut; instead hukumat al-adl.
These cases reinforce the necessity of symmetry.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السنة يمكن اعتبار المماثلة فيهما إلا أن يقطع من الحشفة لأن موضع القطع معلوم فيصار إليه . وعن أبي يوسف أنه إذا قطع من أصلها يجب بخلاف ما إذا قطع بعضها لتعذر اعتبار المماثلة فيه. قال في الينابيع : إذا قطع اليد من العضو والرجل من الفخذ فعندهما فيه الدية، وما فوق الكتف والقدم ففيه حكومة عدل، وعند أبي يوسف : ما فوق الكعب والقدم مع الأصابع . وفي الخلاصة : دية اليد تجب مؤجلة في سنتين ثلثاها في السنة الأولى والباقي في الثانية، وإذا كسر يد عبد رجل أو رجله لا يجب في الحال شيء، ولو قطع أصبعاً زائدة وفي يده مثلها لا قصاص بالإجماع. وقال أبو حنيفة في الاقطعين والأشلين إنه لا قصاص هو قول أبي يوسف في رواية الحسن عنه، وكذلك مقطوع الإبهام أو الأصابع كلها إذا قطع إنسان يده فلا قصاص في قول أبي حنيفة أنه لا قصاص فيه وفيه حكومة عدل.
It is possible to consider similarity in both except if he cuts from the glans because the place of cutting is known, so it is referred to. From Abu Yusuf: If he cuts from its root, it is obligatory; contrary to if he cuts some of it because considering similarity is difficult there. It is said in al-Yanabi': If he cuts the hand from the arm and the foot from the thigh, then according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) there is full diya; for above the shoulder and foot, there is hukumat al-adl. According to Abu Yusuf: for above the ankle and foot with the fingers (he considers differently). In al-Khulasa: The diya of the hand is payable in installments over two years: two-thirds in the first year and the remainder in the second. If he breaks the hand or foot of a slave, nothing is immediately due. If he cuts a superfluous finger while the victim has a similar one (normal), there is no qisas by consensus. Abu Hanifa said regarding the one with a missing hand (aqta') or paralyzed hand (ashall): There is no qisas; this is also the statement of Abu Yusuf in the narration of Hasan from him. Similarly, for one whose thumb or all fingers are already cut off, if someone cuts his (remaining) hand, there is no qisas according to Abu Hanifa, and there is hukumat al-adl.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq discusses rulings on amputations of hands, feet, and fingers. It begins by noting that similarity (mumathala) is considered for qisas in hand and foot cuts, except when the cut is at the glans (possibly meaning the wrist joint) because the exact place is known. Abu Yusuf adds that if the cut is at the root of the hand, qisas is due; if only part, similarity is difficult so no qisas. The text then cites al-Yanabi': When the hand is cut from the arm (above the wrist) or the foot from the thigh, the Hanafi school (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) holds full diya is due; for cuts above the shoulder or foot, hukumat al-adl (equitable compensation determined by a judge) applies. Abu Yusuf further distinguishes: above the ankle (for foot) and foot with fingers require different treatment. The diya for a hand is payable over two years, with two-thirds in the first year and the remainder in the second. A broken hand or foot of a slave does not immediately require compensation. Cutting a supernumerary finger is unanimously not subject to qisas because it is not a standard limb. For a person who already has a missing or paralyzed hand (aqta' or ashal), cutting his remaining hand also does not require qisas due to lack of symmetry; instead, hukumat al-adl applies. These rulings reflect the Hanafi principle that qisas requires precise equivalence, and when that is not possible, financial compensation takes its place.

Key Terms
دية (diya): Financial compensation paid for bodily injuries or homicide, varying by body part.
قصاص (qisas): Retaliation in kind for bodily injuries, requiring precise equivalence (mumathala).
حكومة عدل (hukumat al-adl): Equitable compensation assessed by a judge for injuries where no fixed diya or qisas is prescribed.
اقطع (aqta'): A person whose hand or foot is already amputated (missing).
أشل (ashall): A person with a paralyzed hand or limb.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone cuts off the hand of a person who has a supernumerary finger on that hand, is qisas applicable for the finger?
A) Yes, because any finger cut requires qisas.
B) No, by consensus there is no qisas for a supernumerary finger.
C) Yes, but only if the aggressor also cuts off a normal finger.
D) No, because the finger is not a standard limb; diya is due.

Key Takeaway
Qisas for amputations requires exact symmetry; when symmetry is absent, compensation through diya or hukumat al-adl is substituted.

Bone Breaks and Hukumat al-Adl
General rule for bone fractures

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for breaking a bone and identify the evidence that it incurs hukumat al-adl, not fixed diya.

Core Idea
Breaking a bone like the forearm or shin incurs hukumat al-adl, not a fixed diya.

The Hanafi school specifies fixed diya only for certain injuries. For most bone breaks, the compensation is determined by the judge's assessment. This lesson examines the general rule: any bone break triggers hukumat al-adl.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What injury is described? (Breaking a bone like forearm or shin). What is the compensation? Hukumat al-adl.
2
Understand hukumat al-adl
Hukumat al-adl means the judge uses expert witnesses to assess the loss. It is not a fixed amount.
Contrast with fixed diya for limbs like hands or feet.
3
Note the generality
The phrase 'saa'id aw saq aw ghayrihi' indicates that this applies to any bone break beyond the specific examples.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو كسر عظماً ساعد أو ساق أو غيره ففيه حكومة عدل. وفي ثدي المرأة دية كاملة ولا ذكر له في الكتب. وفي كسر الصلب دية كاملة إن منعه عن الجماع وأحد به فأما إذا لم يحد به ولم يمنعه عن الجماع فهذا على نوعين : إما أن يبقى للجراحة أثر ففيه حكومة عدل ولم يجب كمال الدية، وأما إذا لم يبق لها أثر لم يجب فيه شيء وقد مر هذا فيما تقدم . من وفي الظهيرية : وكذا صدر المرأة إذا انكسر وانقطع الماء منه ففيه الدية، وفي الصلب إذا دق لكن يقدر على الجماع ففيه حكومة عدل وإن لم يقدر وصار أحدب فدية كاملة، وإن عاد إلى حبله ولم ينقص ولكن فيه أثر الضرب ففيه حكومة عدل وإن لم يقدر وصار أحدب فدية كاملة، وإن عاد إلى حبلة ولم ينقص ولكن فيه أثر الضرب ففيه حكومة عدل، وإن لم يكن فيه أثر فلا شيء فيه في قول أبي حنيفة وعندهما تجب أجرة الطبيب، وفي الذكر كمال الدية، وفي ذكر الخصي حكومة عدل سواء كان يتحرك أو لا يقدر الخصي على الوطء أو لا يقدر على هذا الخلاف ذكر العنين. وأما ذكر الشيخ الكبير إن كان يتحرك ولا يقدر على الوطء فالجواب فيه كالجواب في ذكر الخصي وذكر العنين. وفي التهذيب : وفي ذكر الخصي والعينين حكومة عدل وهو ما يرى القاضي بمشورة أهل البصيرة وقيل يقوم أن لو كان عبداً محبوباً وغيره فتجب نسبة النقصان من ديته كما لو نقص عشر القيمة يجب عشر الدية والأول أصح. وفي التجريد: المرأة إذا أفضاها فصارت لا تستمسك البول والغائط أو أحدهما ففيه دية كاملة، وفي الأنثيين كمال الدية.
And if he breaks a bone of the forearm, shin, or other, there is hukumat al-adl. And for the breast of a woman, full diya, and there is no mention of it in the books. And for breaking the spine, full diya if it prevents him from intercourse and makes him hunchbacked. As for if it does not make him hunchbacked and does not prevent intercourse, it is of two types: either the wound leaves a trace, then hukumat al-adl and full diya is not obligatory; or if no trace remains, then nothing is due, and this has passed previously. From al-Zahiriyya: Likewise, the chest of a woman if it breaks and water (milk) stops flowing from it, then full diya. And for the spine if it is crushed but he is capable of intercourse, then hukumat al-adl; if he is not capable and becomes hunchbacked, then full diya. If it returns to its normal state without decrease but there is a trace of the blow, then hukumat al-adl; if he is not capable and becomes hunchbacked, full diya. If it returns to its normal state without decrease but there is a trace of the blow, then hukumat al-adl; if there is no trace, then nothing is due according to Abu Hanifa, while according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) the fee of the physician is obligatory. And for the penis, full diya. For the penis of a eunuch, hukumat al-adl, whether it moves or not, whether the eunuch is capable of intercourse or not; similar difference of opinion is mentioned for the impotent man. As for the penis of an old man, if it moves but he is not capable of intercourse, the answer is the same as for the penis of the eunuch and the impotent. In al-Tahdhib: For the penis of a eunuch and the 'aynayn (impotent?), hukumat al-adl, which is what the judge determines with the consultation of people of insight. It is said that he values him as if he were a beloved slave and others, so the proportion of decrease from his diya becomes obligatory; just as if one-tenth of the value is decreased, one-tenth of the diya is obligatory. The first is more correct. In al-Tajrid: A woman if he makes her incontinent (afda) so that she cannot control urine and feces or one of them, then full diya. And for the two testicles, full diya.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage covers various injuries and their compensations. For breaking a bone like the forearm or shin, hukumat al-adl (equitable compensation) is due, not a fixed diya. A woman's breast has full diya if injured, though this is not mentioned in earlier standard works. For a spinal fracture, full diya is due only if it prevents intercourse and causes hunchback; otherwise, if there is a trace, hukumat al-adl; if no trace, nothing. The Zahiriyya adds that if a woman's chest breaks and milk flow stops, full diya is due. For a crushed spine where the person can still have intercourse, hukumat al-adl; if he cannot and becomes hunchbacked, full diya. If the spine returns to normal with no decrease but a trace remains, hukumat al-adl; if no trace, Abu Hanifa says nothing, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say the cost of medical treatment is due. The penis carries full diya. However, for a eunuch's penis, only hukumat al-adl is due, regardless of movement or ability to have intercourse. Similarly for an impotent man and an old man who cannot have intercourse. The Tahdhib explains that hukumat al-adl is determined by a judge consulting experts. There is also a view that the decrease in value is proportionate to diya, but the first (judge's discretion) is more correct. Finally, if a man causes a woman to become incontinent (afda), preventing control of urine and feces, full diya is due; likewise for the two testicles, full diya.

Key Terms
حكومة عدل (hukumat al-adl): Equitable compensation determined by a judge with expert consultation, for injuries without a fixed diya.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the compensation for breaking a bone like the forearm or shin according to the Hanafi school?
A) Full diya
B) Half diya
C) Hukumat al-adl
D) Nothing if it heals

Key Takeaway
Any bone break incurs hukumat al-adl, not a fixed diya.

Breast, Chest, and Spine Injuries – Graded Diya
Diya and hukumat for breast, chest, spine

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the graded diya rules for breast, chest, and spine injuries, distinguishing between full diya and hukumat al-adl.

Core Idea
Full diya is due for a woman's breast and for spinal fractures causing paralysis; hukumat for lesser spinal injuries.

This lesson covers three body parts with varying compensation. A woman's breast and a chest fracture stopping milk production both incur full diya. Spinal injuries are graded: full diya if it prevents intercourse and causes hunchback, otherwise hukumat al-adl if a trace remains, or nothing if no trace. There is also an intra-Hanafi disagreement on the doctor's fee when no trace remains.

Guided Path
1
Classify each injury
List: breast, chest, spine. Identify whether each has a fixed diya or hukumat.
2
Analyze spinal conditions
Break down the conditions: did it cause hunchback? Prevent intercourse? Does a trace remain? Each combination yields a different ruling.
Trace means visible scar or deformity.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa says nothing if no trace; Sahibayn require the injurer to pay the doctor's fee.
This is a minor difference in practical outcome.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو كسر عظماً ساعد أو ساق أو غيره ففيه حكومة عدل. وفي ثدي المرأة دية كاملة ولا ذكر له في الكتب. وفي كسر الصلب دية كاملة إن منعه عن الجماع وأحد به فأما إذا لم يحد به ولم يمنعه عن الجماع فهذا على نوعين : إما أن يبقى للجراحة أثر ففيه حكومة عدل ولم يجب كمال الدية، وأما إذا لم يبق لها أثر لم يجب فيه شيء وقد مر هذا فيما تقدم . من وفي الظهيرية : وكذا صدر المرأة إذا انكسر وانقطع الماء منه ففيه الدية، وفي الصلب إذا دق لكن يقدر على الجماع ففيه حكومة عدل وإن لم يقدر وصار أحدب فدية كاملة، وإن عاد إلى حبله ولم ينقص ولكن فيه أثر الضرب ففيه حكومة عدل وإن لم يقدر وصار أحدب فدية كاملة، وإن عاد إلى حبلة ولم ينقص ولكن فيه أثر الضرب ففيه حكومة عدل، وإن لم يكن فيه أثر فلا شيء فيه في قول أبي حنيفة وعندهما تجب أجرة الطبيب، وفي الذكر كمال الدية، وفي ذكر الخصي حكومة عدل سواء كان يتحرك أو لا يقدر الخصي على الوطء أو لا يقدر على هذا الخلاف ذكر العنين. وأما ذكر الشيخ الكبير إن كان يتحرك ولا يقدر على الوطء فالجواب فيه كالجواب في ذكر الخصي وذكر العنين. وفي التهذيب : وفي ذكر الخصي والعينين حكومة عدل وهو ما يرى القاضي بمشورة أهل البصيرة وقيل يقوم أن لو كان عبداً محبوباً وغيره فتجب نسبة النقصان من ديته كما لو نقص عشر القيمة يجب عشر الدية والأول أصح. وفي التجريد: المرأة إذا أفضاها فصارت لا تستمسك البول والغائط أو أحدهما ففيه دية كاملة، وفي الأنثيين كمال الدية.

Key Terms
ثدي (thady): Woman's breast; injury to it incurs full diya.
صلب (sulb): Spine; graded diya based on consequences.

Key Terms from Source Passage

According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling for a spinal fracture that prevents intercourse and causes hunchback?
A) Hukumat al-adl
B) Full diya
C) Half diya

Key Takeaway
Full diya for spinal injury only if it causes both hunchback and inability to have intercourse.

Male Genital Injuries – Penis, Testicles, and Special Cases
Diya and hukumat for male genitalia

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when full diya applies to male genital injuries and when hukumat al-adl is used instead.

Core Idea
Full diya for penis and testicles; hukumat for eunuch's or impotent man's penis.

This lesson distinguishes between different male genital injuries. The penis and testicles have full diya. However, for a eunuch (castrated) or impotent man, the penis incurs only hukumat al-adl because it lacks full function. The valuation method for hukumat is also discussed: the judge's assessment is preferred over a proportional calculation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default ruling
For the penis and testicles, full diya is wajib. This is the baseline.
2
Recognize exceptions
For a eunuch (castrated) and an impotent man ('anin), the penis incurs hukumat al-adl even if it can move.
The key is lack of reproductive function.
3
Understand the valuation debate
Two methods: (1) judge's consultation with experts (preferred); (2) proportional valuation of the slave, then proportion of diya.
The text says the first is more correct.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو كسر عظماً ساعد أو ساق أو غيره ففيه حكومة عدل. وفي ثدي المرأة دية كاملة ولا ذكر له في الكتب. وفي كسر الصلب دية كاملة إن منعه عن الجماع وأحد به فأما إذا لم يحد به ولم يمنعه عن الجماع فهذا على نوعين : إما أن يبقى للجراحة أثر ففيه حكومة عدل ولم يجب كمال الدية، وأما إذا لم يبق لها أثر لم يجب فيه شيء وقد مر هذا فيما تقدم . من وفي الظهيرية : وكذا صدر المرأة إذا انكسر وانقطع الماء منه ففيه الدية، وفي الصلب إذا دق لكن يقدر على الجماع ففيه حكومة عدل وإن لم يقدر وصار أحدب فدية كاملة، وإن عاد إلى حبله ولم ينقص ولكن فيه أثر الضرب ففيه حكومة عدل وإن لم يقدر وصار أحدب فدية كاملة، وإن عاد إلى حبلة ولم ينقص ولكن فيه أثر الضرب ففيه حكومة عدل، وإن لم يكن فيه أثر فلا شيء فيه في قول أبي حنيفة وعندهما تجب أجرة الطبيب، وفي الذكر كمال الدية، وفي ذكر الخصي حكومة عدل سواء كان يتحرك أو لا يقدر الخصي على الوطء أو لا يقدر على هذا الخلاف ذكر العنين. وأما ذكر الشيخ الكبير إن كان يتحرك ولا يقدر على الوطء فالجواب فيه كالجواب في ذكر الخصي وذكر العنين. وفي التهذيب : وفي ذكر الخصي والعينين حكومة عدل وهو ما يرى القاضي بمشورة أهل البصيرة وقيل يقوم أن لو كان عبداً محبوباً وغيره فتجب نسبة النقصان من ديته كما لو نقص عشر القيمة يجب عشر الدية والأول أصح. وفي التجريد: المرأة إذا أفضاها فصارت لا تستمسك البول والغائط أو أحدهما ففيه دية كاملة، وفي الأنثيين كمال الدية.
And if he breaks a bone of the forearm, shin, or other, there is hukumat al-adl. And for the breast of a woman, full diya, and there is no mention of it in the books. And for breaking the spine, full diya if it prevents him from intercourse and makes him hunchbacked. As for if it does not make him hunchbacked and does not prevent intercourse, it is of two types: either the wound leaves a trace, then hukumat al-adl and full diya is not obligatory; or if no trace remains, then nothing is due, and this has passed previously. From al-Zahiriyya: Likewise, the chest of a woman if it breaks and water (milk) stops flowing from it, then full diya. And for the spine if it is crushed but he is capable of intercourse, then hukumat al-adl; if he is not capable and becomes hunchbacked, then full diya. If it returns to its normal state without decrease but there is a trace of the blow, then hukumat al-adl; if he is not capable and becomes hunchbacked, full diya. If it returns to its normal state without decrease but there is a trace of the blow, then hukumat al-adl; if there is no trace, then nothing is due according to Abu Hanifa, while according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) the fee of the physician is obligatory. And for the penis, full diya. For the penis of a eunuch, hukumat al-adl, whether it moves or not, whether the eunuch is capable of intercourse or not; similar difference of opinion is mentioned for the impotent man. As for the penis of an old man, if it moves but he is not capable of intercourse, the answer is the same as for the penis of the eunuch and the impotent. In al-Tahdhib: For the penis of a eunuch and the 'aynayn (impotent?), hukumat al-adl, which is what the judge determines with the consultation of people of insight. It is said that he values him as if he were a beloved slave and others, so the proportion of decrease from his diya becomes obligatory; just as if one-tenth of the value is decreased, one-tenth of the diya is obligatory. The first is more correct. In al-Tajrid: A woman if he makes her incontinent (afda) so that she cannot control urine and feces or one of them, then full diya. And for the two testicles, full diya.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage covers various injuries and their compensations. For breaking a bone like the forearm or shin, hukumat al-adl (equitable compensation) is due, not a fixed diya. A woman's breast has full diya if injured, though this is not mentioned in earlier standard works. For a spinal fracture, full diya is due only if it prevents intercourse and causes hunchback; otherwise, if there is a trace, hukumat al-adl; if no trace, nothing. The Zahiriyya adds that if a woman's chest breaks and milk flow stops, full diya is due. For a crushed spine where the person can still have intercourse, hukumat al-adl; if he cannot and becomes hunchbacked, full diya. If the spine returns to normal with no decrease but a trace remains, hukumat al-adl; if no trace, Abu Hanifa says nothing, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say the cost of medical treatment is due. The penis carries full diya. However, for a eunuch's penis, only hukumat al-adl is due, regardless of movement or ability to have intercourse. Similarly for an impotent man and an old man who cannot have intercourse. The Tahdhib explains that hukumat al-adl is determined by a judge consulting experts. There is also a view that the decrease in value is proportionate to diya, but the first (judge's discretion) is more correct. Finally, if a man causes a woman to become incontinent (afda), preventing control of urine and feces, full diya is due; likewise for the two testicles, full diya.

Key Terms
خصي (khasi): A eunuch; a castrated male.
عنين ('anin): An impotent man who cannot achieve intercourse.
ذكر (dhakar): Penis; carries full diya for normal men.
الأنثيين (al-uthyayn): The two testicles; full diya for injury.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the compensation for injury to a eunuch's penis?
A) Full diya
B) Hukumat al-adl
C) Half diya
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
Full diya for penis only in men with normal reproductive capacity; eunuchs and impotent men incur hukumat.

Afda (Incontinence) and Hukumat Valuation Method
Ruling on afda and valuation method

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for afda (causing incontinence) and explain the preferred method for hukumat valuation.

Core Idea
Causing a woman to become incontinent (afda) incurs full diya; hukumat valuation by judge's experts is preferred over proportional calculation.

This lesson covers two separate but related points: first, the ruling for afda—when a man causes a woman to lose control of urine and/or feces, full diya is due. Second, the valuation method for hukumat al-adl in general: the judge's consultation of experts is the relied-upon method, rather than a proportional assessment based on slave value.

Guided Path
1
Understand afda
Afda means making a woman incontinent, unable to control urine or feces. It carries full diya.
2
Identify the valuation dispute
Two methods exist: judge's discretion with experts (preferred) vs. proportional reduction of diya based on loss of value.
The text says the first is more correct.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Compensation for Cutting the Penis: Glans and Remainder
Diya for penis cuts with healing condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the diya for cutting the glans and apply the healing condition to determine compensation for the remainder of the penis.

Core Idea
Cutting the glans alone incurs full diya; cutting the rest after healing triggers only hukumat, not a second diya.

This lesson addresses the compensation for cutting the penis, focusing on the distinction between cutting the glans alone and cutting the rest of the penis, and the crucial role of healing between injuries. Understanding this distinction is essential for accurate diya calculations in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is cutting the glans (hashafa). The ruling is that full diya is wajib (obligatory).
Full diya is the complete blood money, typically 100 camels or equivalent.
2
Determine if a second cut occurs
If the rest of the penis is cut after the glans, check whether the first wound healed (bar') before the second cut.
Healing is determined by complete closure of the wound and return of normal function.
3
Apply the healing condition
If no healing intervened, treat as one stroke: full diya for the entire penis. If healing occurred, full diya for the glans plus hukumat al-adl (equitable assessment) for the remainder.
Hukumat al-adl is determined by a qadi based on the extent of loss.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا قطع الحشفة يجب كمال الدية فإن قطع باقي الذكر فإن كان قبل تخلل البرء تجب دية كاملة ويجعل كأنه قطع الذكر بدفعة واحدة، وإن تخلل بينهما برء فيجب كمال الدية في الحشفة وحكومة العدل في الباقي. وإذا قطع الذكر والأنثيين من الرجل الصحيح خطأ إن بدأ بقطع الذكر ففيه ديتان. وفي التجريد: وكذا إذا قطعها من جانب واحد ولو بدأ بقطع الأنثيين ثم بالذكر ففي الانثيين الدية كاملة وفي الذكر حكومة عدل، وإن قطعهما من جانب الفخذ معاً فعليه ديتان وفي التحفة : وفي الأنثيين إذا قطعهما مع الذكر جملة واحدة في حالة واحدة يجب عليه ديتان : دية بإزاء الذكر ودية بإزاء الأنثيين. وإذا قطع الذكر أولاً ثم الأنثيين يجب ديتان أيضاً لأن بقطع الذكر قطع منفعة الأنثيين وهي إمساك المني، فأما إذا قطع الأنثيين أولاً ثم الذكر تجب الدية بقطع الأنثيين وتجب بقطع الذكر حكومة العدل، وفي الإليتين إذا قطعتا خطأ كمال الدية. وفي الظهيرية : وفي أحدهما نصف الدية. وفي المنتقى عن محمد : إذا قطع إحدى أنثييه وانقطع ماؤه دية ونصف قال: ولا نعلم ذهاب الماء إلا باقرار الجاني فإذا قطع الباقي من إحدى الأنثيين يجب نصف الدية. ولم يذكر في الكتاب الحكم في العمد والظاهر الأنثيين أنه يجب فيه القصاص حالة العمد
And if he cuts the glans, full diya is obligatory. Then if he cuts the rest of the penis, if it was before healing (of the first cut) intervened, full diya is due and it is considered as if he cut the penis in one stroke. But if healing intervened between them, then full diya is due for the glans and hukumat al-adl for the remainder. And if he cuts the penis and the two testicles of a healthy man by mistake, if he began with cutting the penis, then there are two full diyas. In al-Tajrid: Likewise if he cuts them from one side, and if he began with cutting the testicles then the penis, then for the testicles full diya and for the penis hukumat al-adl. And if he cuts both from the thigh side together, then two diyas are due. In al-Tuhfa: For the testicles if he cuts them together with the penis in a single action in one state, two diyas are due: a diya for the penis and a diya for the testicles. And if he cuts the penis first then the testicles, two diyas are also due because by cutting the penis, he cuts off the benefit of the testicles, which is retention of semen. As for if he cuts the testicles first then the penis, then diya is due for cutting the testicles and hukumat al-adl for cutting the penis. And for the buttocks, if cut by mistake, full diya. In al-Zahiriyya: For one of them, half diya. In al-Muntaqa from Muhammad: If he cuts one of his testicles and his semen ceases, then diya and a half. He said: We only know cessation of semen by the confession of the offender. Then if he cuts the remaining one of the testicles, half diya is due. And the book did not mention the ruling in case of intentional (injury), but apparently for testicles, qisas is obligatory in case of intentional injury.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage details compensation for cuts to the male genitalia. Cutting just the glans (head of the penis) requires full diya. If the cut extends to the rest of the penis, the ruling depends on whether the initial cut had healed. If no healing intervened, it is treated as one incident and full diya for the entire penis is due. If healing occurred between cuts, then full diya for the glans and hukumat al-adl for the remainder. When both penis and testicles are cut mistakenly, the number of diyas depends on the order: if the penis is cut first, two full diyas (one for each organ). If testicles first, then full diya for testicles and hukumat for penis. If both are cut simultaneously from the side of the thigh, two full diyas. The Tuhfa confirms that simultaneous cutting of both in one action requires two diyas. Cutting the buttocks mistakenly incurs full diya; for one buttock, half diya. Muhammad in al-Muntaqa adds that if one testicle is cut and semen ceases, then diya and a half (i.e., full diya for loss of testicle plus half for loss of function). The cessation of semen is only known by the offender's confession. If the remaining testicle is then cut, half diya is due. The text notes that the ruling in the book (likely Kanz al-Daqa'iq) does not discuss intentional injury to testicles, but the apparent ruling is that qisas applies in intentional cases.

Key Terms
حشفة (hashafa): The glans (head) of the penis.
برء (bar'): Healing of a wound.
حكومة العدل (hukumat al-adl): Equitable assessment of compensation by a qadi when diya is not fixed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone cuts the glans and then cuts the rest of the penis after the glans wound has completely healed, what is the compensation?
A) Full diya for the entire penis
B) Full diya for the glans and hukumat for the remainder
C) Two full diyas
D) Only hukumat for both

Key Takeaway
When the penis is cut in two separate incidents with healing intervening, full diya is due only for the glans, and the remainder receives hukumat.

Multiple Diyas: Cutting Penis and Testicles
Diya for combined penis and testicle cuts with order consideration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to derive the number of diyas owed when both the penis and testicles are cut, based on the order of severance.

Core Idea
Cutting both penis and testicles incurs two diyas if the penis is cut first or simultaneously; if testicles first, one diya plus hukumat for the penis.

When both the penis and testicles are cut by mistake, the number of diyas depends on the order of severance. The Hanafi school provides detailed rulings for sequential and simultaneous cuts, reflecting the principle that each organ's independent compensation applies unless the order affects the function of the other.

Guided Path
1
Identify the organs involved
The two organs are the penis and the two testicles. The testicles are considered a pair; cutting both is equivalent to one loss of the pair.
The text mentions 'الأنثيين' (the two testicles) as a unit.
2
Consider the order of cutting
There are three possibilities: (1) penis first, then testicles; (2) testicles first, then penis; (3) both in one action.
3
Apply the rule for each order
For penis first: two full diyas (one for penis, one for testicles) because cutting the penis severs the benefit of the testicles (semen retention). For testicles first: full diya for testicles plus hukumat for penis. For simultaneous: two full diyas.
If both are cut from the thigh side together, two diyas are also due per al-Tajrid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And if he cuts the glans, full diya is obligatory. Then if he cuts the rest of the penis, if it was before healing (of the first cut) intervened, full diya is due and it is considered as if he cut the penis in one stroke. But if healing intervened between them, then full diya is due for the glans and hukumat al-adl for the remainder. And if he cuts the penis and the two testicles of a healthy man by mistake, if he began with cutting the penis, then there are two full diyas. In al-Tajrid: Likewise if he cuts them from one side, and if he began with cutting the testicles then the penis, then for the testicles full diya and for the penis hukumat al-adl. And if he cuts both from the thigh side together, then two diyas are due. In al-Tuhfa: For the testicles if he cuts them together with the penis in a single action in one state, two diyas are due: a diya for the penis and a diya for the testicles. And if he cuts the penis first then the testicles, two diyas are also due because by cutting the penis, he cuts off the benefit of the testicles, which is retention of semen. As for if he cuts the testicles first then the penis, then diya is due for cutting the testicles and hukumat al-adl for cutting the penis. And for the buttocks, if cut by mistake, full diya. In al-Zahiriyya: For one of them, half diya. In al-Muntaqa from Muhammad: If he cuts one of his testicles and his semen ceases, then diya and a half. He said: We only know cessation of semen by the confession of the offender. Then if he cuts the remaining one of the testicles, half diya is due. And the book did not mention the ruling in case of intentional (injury), but apparently for testicles, qisas is obligatory in case of intentional injury.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage details compensation for cuts to the male genitalia. Cutting just the glans (head of the penis) requires full diya. If the cut extends to the rest of the penis, the ruling depends on whether the initial cut had healed. If no healing intervened, it is treated as one incident and full diya for the entire penis is due. If healing occurred between cuts, then full diya for the glans and hukumat al-adl for the remainder. When both penis and testicles are cut mistakenly, the number of diyas depends on the order: if the penis is cut first, two full diyas (one for each organ). If testicles first, then full diya for testicles and hukumat for penis. If both are cut simultaneously from the side of the thigh, two full diyas. The Tuhfa confirms that simultaneous cutting of both in one action requires two diyas. Cutting the buttocks mistakenly incurs full diya; for one buttock, half diya. Muhammad in al-Muntaqa adds that if one testicle is cut and semen ceases, then diya and a half (i.e., full diya for loss of testicle plus half for loss of function). The cessation of semen is only known by the offender's confession. If the remaining testicle is then cut, half diya is due. The text notes that the ruling in the book (likely Kanz al-Daqa'iq) does not discuss intentional injury to testicles, but the apparent ruling is that qisas applies in intentional cases.

Key Terms
أنثيين (unthayayn): The two testicles.
إمساك المني (imsak al-maniyy): Retention of semen, a function of the penis that depends on testicles.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, if the testicles are cut first and then the penis, what is the compensation?
A) Two full diyas
B) Full diya for testicles and hukumat for penis
C) Full diya for penis and hukumat for testicles
D) Nothing because the testicles were first

Key Takeaway
The number of diyas for combined penis and testicle injuries depends on the order of severance: two diyas if penis first or simultaneous, one diya plus hukumat if testicles first.

Diya for Testicles and Buttocks: Special Cases
Diya for testicle function loss and buttock cuts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate diya for cutting one testicle with loss of function, and for cutting the buttocks.

Core Idea
Loss of function from testicle injury adds half diya; cutting both buttocks incurs full diya, one buttock half.

In addition to the general rules, the Hanafi school addresses special cases: when one testicle is cut and the victim loses the ability to produce semen, an extra half diya is due. Additionally, cutting the buttocks has fixed diya amounts. This lesson covers these exceptional rulings and the evidentiary requirement for function loss.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario for testicles
The first scenario: cutting one testicle with proven loss of semen production. The second: cutting the remaining testicle after the first was already removed with function loss.
Loss of function is known only by the offender's confession (iqrar).
2
Apply diya for one testicle with function loss
For cutting one testicle with cessation of semen, diya and a half are due: full diya for the testicle plus half diya for loss of function.
This is from al-Muntaqa from Muhammad.
3
Apply diya for cutting the remaining testicle
If after the first loss, the other testicle is cut, only half diya is due because the function was already lost.
The half diya is for the organ itself.
4
Apply diya for buttocks
Cutting both buttocks by mistake incurs full diya; cutting one buttock incurs half diya.
From al-Zahiriyya.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا قطع الحشفة يجب كمال الدية فإن قطع باقي الذكر فإن كان قبل تخلل البرء تجب دية كاملة ويجعل كأنه قطع الذكر بدفعة واحدة، وإن تخلل بينهما برء فيجب كمال الدية في الحشفة وحكومة العدل في الباقي. وإذا قطع الذكر والأنثيين من الرجل الصحيح خطأ إن بدأ بقطع الذكر ففيه ديتان. وفي التجريد: وكذا إذا قطعها من جانب واحد ولو بدأ بقطع الأنثيين ثم بالذكر ففي الانثيين الدية كاملة وفي الذكر حكومة عدل، وإن قطعهما من جانب الفخذ معاً فعليه ديتان وفي التحفة : وفي الأنثيين إذا قطعهما مع الذكر جملة واحدة في حالة واحدة يجب عليه ديتان : دية بإزاء الذكر ودية بإزاء الأنثيين. وإذا قطع الذكر أولاً ثم الأنثيين يجب ديتان أيضاً لأن بقطع الذكر قطع منفعة الأنثيين وهي إمساك المني، فأما إذا قطع الأنثيين أولاً ثم الذكر تجب الدية بقطع الأنثيين وتجب بقطع الذكر حكومة العدل، وفي الإليتين إذا قطعتا خطأ كمال الدية. وفي الظهيرية : وفي أحدهما نصف الدية. وفي المنتقى عن محمد : إذا قطع إحدى أنثييه وانقطع ماؤه دية ونصف قال: ولا نعلم ذهاب الماء إلا باقرار الجاني فإذا قطع الباقي من إحدى الأنثيين يجب نصف الدية. ولم يذكر في الكتاب الحكم في العمد والظاهر الأنثيين أنه يجب فيه القصاص حالة العمد
And if he cuts the glans, full diya is obligatory. Then if he cuts the rest of the penis, if it was before healing (of the first cut) intervened, full diya is due and it is considered as if he cut the penis in one stroke. But if healing intervened between them, then full diya is due for the glans and hukumat al-adl for the remainder. And if he cuts the penis and the two testicles of a healthy man by mistake, if he began with cutting the penis, then there are two full diyas. Diya and Qisas for Foot, Leg, and Coital Injuries
Diya and qisas for foot/leg injuries and coital injuries

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the diya amounts for foot and leg injuries, identify when qisas applies, explain the principle for healed bones, and describe the intra-Hanafi dispute on diya for coital incontinence.

Core Idea
Compensation for injury is prescribed: full diya for feet, qisas at joints, no payment for healed bones, and a dispute between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf on diya for incontinence.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq outlines the specific compensations for injuries to the feet, legs, and coital areas. It details diya amounts, conditions for qisas, and the general principle that no compensation is due for bones that heal without defect. The passage also records an intra-Hanafi disagreement over diya for a woman made incontinent by intercourse.

Guided Path
1
Classify the injury
Determine if the injury is to a foot, leg, toe, or coital area. For bones, check if it healed completely or left a defect.
Body part and severity determine the compensation.
2
Identify the mode of injury
Is it intentional or mistaken? This distinguishes qisas from diya.
Qisas only for intentional amputation at a joint.
3
Locate the compensation rule
Find the specific ruling: full diya for foot, half for one, tenth per toe; qisas for intentional cut at joint; no diya for healed bone; hukumat for defect; full diya for incontinence due to injury.
Each injury has a defined amount or condition.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute
For coital incontinence (afda') caused by consensual intercourse, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say no diya; Abu Yusuf says full or one-third diya.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الرجلين كمال الدية في الخطأ، وفي أحدهما نصف الدية، وفي كل أصبع من أصابع الرجلين عشر الدية، وفي الرجل في العمد القصاص إذا قطع من مفصل القدم أو من مفصل الركبة أو من مفصل الورك، وإن قطعت من غير المفصل لا يجب القصاص. وفي الذخيرة : وكذلك الحكم في أصابع الرجلين إن قطع من المفصل عمداً يجب القصاص، وإذا قطع الرجل خطأ من نصف الساق تجب الدية لأجل القدم وحكومة العدل فيما وراء القدم والكلام فيه نظير الكلام في اليد إذا قطعت من نصف الساعد. وإن كسر فخذه فبرأت واستقامت فلا شيء عليه، وفي قول أبي يوسف حكومة عدل، وذكر أبو سليمان عن محمد في كتاب الخراج قال أبو حنيفة : ما انكسر من إنسان يداً أو رجلاً أو غير ذلك وبرىء وعاد كهيئته فليس فيه عقل، وإن كان فيه نقص بأن برىء العظم وبقي فيه ورم ففيه من عقله بحساب ما نقص، وكذلك في الجراحة الجسد إذا برأ وعاد كهيئة فليس فيه شيء. ولو كان في شيء ذلك من شلل ففيه حكومة عدل إلا الجائفة فإن فيها ثلث دية النفس، وإذا طعن برمح أو غيره في دبره وصار لا يستمسك الطعام في جوفه ففيه الدية، وإذا ضرب فسلسل بوله وصار بحال لا يستمسكه ففيه الدية، وإذا ضرب فقطع فرج امرأة وصارت يحال لا يمكن جماعها ففيه الدية. وفي الينابيع : وكذا لو قطع فرجها من الجانبين حتى وصل إلى العظم، وإن قطع أحدهما ففيه نصف الدية. وفي فتاوى سمرق رقند : فإن جامع امرأة لا يجامع مثلها فماتت فعلى عاقلته ديتها . وفي جنايات المنتقى : إذا جامع امرأة فأفضاها حتى لا تستمسك البول فلا شيء عليه وهذا قول أبي حنيفة ومحمد وقال أبو يوسف : إن كانت لا تستمسك البول فعليه الدية في ماله، وإن كانت تستمسك فعليه ثلث الدية وفي الكبرى : وإن كانت بحيث تستمسك ففيها ثلث الدية وفي فتاوى الخلاصة : رجل جامع صغيرة لا يجامع مثلها فماتت، فإن كانت أجنبية فالدية على العاقلة، وإن كانت منكوحته فالدية على العاقلة والمهر على الزوج، ولو أزال بكارة امرأة بالحجر أو غيره يجب المهر . وفي الينابيع : وإن زني بها مطاوعة وأفضاها فلا شيء عليه عندهما. وقال أبو يوسف: تجب الدية على عاقلته وفي الينابيع : وإذا ضرب امرأة فأقضاها وصارت بحيث لا
And for the two feet, full diya in mistake, and for one of them half diya, and for each toe of the two feet one-tenth of diya. For the foot in intentional injury, qisas is obligatory if he cuts from the ankle joint or from the knee joint or from the hip joint. But if he cuts from other than the joint, qisas is not obligatory. In al-Dhakhira: Likewise the ruling for toes of the two feet: if he cuts from the joint intentionally, qisas is obligatory. And if he cuts the foot mistakenly from halfway up the shin, then diya is due for the foot and hukumat al-adl for what is above the foot, and the discussion is similar to that of the hand if cut from halfway up the forearm. And if he breaks his thigh and it heals and becomes straight, then nothing is due. In the statement of Abu Yusuf, hukumat al-adl. Abu Sulayman narrated from Muhammad in Kitab al-Kharaj that Abu Hanifa said: Whatever bone of a person is broken, whether hand, foot, or other, and heals and returns to its original condition, then there is no 'aql (diya) for it. But if there is a deficiency, such as the bone heals but a swelling remains, then there is from its 'aql according to the extent of the deficiency. Similarly, for bodily wounds, if it heals and returns to its original state, there is nothing. And if there is paralysis in any of that, then hukumat al-adl, except for the penetrating wound (ja'ifa) which carries one-third of the full diya. And if he stabs with a spear or other in his anus and he becomes unable to retain food in his stomach, then full diya is due. And if he strikes so that he becomes incontinent of urine and cannot retain it, then full diya. And if he strikes and cuts the vulva of a woman so that she becomes unable to be penetrated, then full diya. In al-Yanabi': Likewise if he cuts her vulva from both sides until reaching the bone, and if he cuts one side, then half diya. In Fatawa Samarqand: If a man has intercourse with a woman who is not customarily penetrable (e.g., too young) and she dies, then her diya is upon his 'aaqila (tribe). In Jinaayat al-Muntaqa: If he has intercourse with a woman and makes her incontinent (afda) so that she cannot retain urine, then nothing is due; this is the statement of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: If she cannot retain urine, then diya is due from his property; if she can retain it, then one-third diya. In al-Kubra: If she can retain it, then one-third diya. In Fatawa al-Khulasa: A man had intercourse with a minor who is not customarily penetrable and she died: if she was a stranger, diya is on the 'aaqila; if she was his wife, diya is on the 'aaqila and the mahr is on the husband. And if he removed the hymen of a woman with a stone or other, the mahr is obligatory. In al-Yanabi': And if he commits zina with her willingly and makes her incontinent, then nothing is due according to them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). Abu Yusuf said: Diya is obligatory on his 'aaqila. And in al-Yanabi': And if he strikes a woman and makes her fadha (incontinent?) so that she becomes unable to...
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage concludes with rulings on foot and leg injuries, then shifts to coital injuries. For the two feet, full diya if amputated by mistake; for one foot, half diya; each toe is one-tenth. Intentional amputation at the ankle, knee, or hip joint requires qisas; otherwise not. The same applies to toes. If the foot is cut from mid-shin by mistake, diya for the foot and hukumat for the rest. A broken thigh that heals straight incurs nothing; Abu Yusuf says hukumat. Abu Hanifa's general principle: a broken bone that heals to its original state has no diya; if a defect remains (e.g., swelling), compensation proportionate to the defect. For paralysis, hukumat except for ja'ifa (penetrating wound to trunk) which is one-third diya. Stabbing in the anus causing loss of fecal control, or striking causing urinary incontinence, or cutting the vulva to prevent intercourse all incur full diya. Cutting the vulva from both sides to the bone incurs full diya; one side half. Coital injuries: If a man has intercourse with a woman who is not normally penetrable (e.g., due to young age) and she dies, diya on his 'aaqila. If intercourse causes incontinence (afda'), Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say nothing, while Abu Yusuf says full diya if she cannot retain urine, one-third if she can. For a minor wife who dies from intercourse, diya on 'aaqila and mahr on husband. Removing hymen with a stone requires mahr. For zina with a willing woman causing incontinence, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say nothing; Abu Yusuf says diya on 'aaqila.

Key Terms
أفضاها (afdaha): To make a woman incontinent by tearing the partition between vagina and rectum/bladder.
عاقلة ('aaqila): The tribal group or relatives who pay diya on behalf of a killer or injurer.
جائفة (ja'ifa): A wound that penetrates into the body cavity (belly, chest, etc.).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, if a man has consensual intercourse with a woman and causes incontinence (afda'), what compensation is due?
A) Full diya
B) One-third diya
C) Nothing
D) Hukumat al-adl

Key Takeaway
Compensation for injury varies: full diya for feet, qisas at joints, no payment for healed bones, and an intra-Hanafi dispute on diya for coital incontinence.

Diyat — Blood Money

Settlement for an Accidental Wound: Effect of Subsequent Death
Fatwa on settlement for accidental wound leading to death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on whether a settlement for an accidental wound covers future death and apply the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
A settlement for a wound does not automatically cover death unless agreed.

When a person settles for an accidental wound and the victim later dies, does the settlement stand? The Hanafi school has an internal difference. This lesson walks through Abu Yusuf's fatwa in al-Jami' and the views of Abu Hanifa and the two Sahibayn.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
A wounder (shajj) pays a settlement for an accidental mudiha wound; later the victim dies from that wound. What happens to the settlement and who pays diya?
2
State Abu Yusuf's ruling in al-Jami'
Abu Yusuf rules: one-third is deducted from the 'aqila (they pay two-thirds of diya), the settlement is void, and the wounder gets back his payment.
This is recorded in al-Jami', a trusted source though not Zahir al-Riwayah.
3
Recognize the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa holds that settlement does not cover future death – so if death occurs, the settlement is like it never existed, and full diya is on the 'aqila. The Sahibayn agree with the one-third deduction.
The source explicitly says this answer is 'ala qawlihima khasatan – specific to the Sahibayn.
4
Identify the mufta bihi
Later fatwa prefers the Sahibayn's view: settlement partially stands (one-third deducted) and the wounder recovers his payment.
Al-Marghinani and others adopt this as the operative position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعن أبي يوسف في جامع : إذا صالح الشاج من موضحة الخطأ على خمسمائة درهم ثم مات منها يحط عن العاقلة الثلث وبطل الصلح ويرجع الشاج بما دفع. وفي الكبرى : وهذا الجواب على قولهما خاصة، أما على قول أبي حنيفة فالصلح والعفو عن الشجة لا يتناول ما يحدث منها، فإذا مات المشجوج ها هنا صار وجود الصلح كعدمه عنده، ولو انعدم الصلح عنده فالدية على عاقلة الشاج كذا هنا. وفي الظهيرية : وإن وقع الصلح على خمسة عشر ألفاً بعد قضاء القاضي بعشرة آلاف فهذا الصلح باطل لما فيه من الزيادة على الدية، وإن كان مائة المقضي به من الإبل فاصطلحا على مائة وخمسين إن وقع الصلح نسيئة لا شك أنه لا يجوز، وإن كان يداً بيد إن كان الإبل بأعيانها ثم اصطلحوا على مائة وخمسين من الإبل بأعيانها كان ذلك جائزاً هذا إذا وقع الصلح على أكثر من النوع الذي وقع به القضاء، أما إذا وقع الصلح على أقل مما وقع به القضاء فإنه يجوز حالاً ونسيئة، وإذا اصطلحا على خلاف جنس ما وقع به القضاء وقد صالحه على أكثر مما قضى به فإنه يجوز. هذا الذي ذكرنا إذا اصطلحا بعد القضاء أو الرضا، أما إذا اصطلحا قبل القضاء إن كان المصالح عليه أكثر من الدية فإنه لا يجوز. ابن سماعة عن محمد في رجل جرحه رجلان جراحة عمداً فقضى بالقصاص على أحدهما ثم مات من الجراحتين قال : لورثته أن يقتلوا الآخر، ولو جرحه رجل
And from Abu Yusuf in al-Jami': If the wounder settles for an accidental head wound for five hundred dirhams, then the victim dies from it, one-third is deducted from the 'aqila, the settlement is void, and the wounder takes back what he paid. In al-Kubra: This answer is specifically according to the two Sahibayn. As for Abu Hanifa's view, settlement and forgiveness for the wound do not cover what results from it. So when the wounded dies here, the existence of the settlement is like its non-existence according to him. If settlement ceased according to him, then the diya is upon the 'aqila of the wounder. Likewise here. In al-Zahiriyya: If settlement occurred on fifteen thousand after the qadi's ruling of ten thousand, this settlement is void because of the increase over the diya. If the ruled amount was one hundred camels, and they settled on one hundred fifty, if the settlement was deferred, there is no doubt it is not permissible. If it was hand-to-hand, and the camels were specific, then they settled on one hundred fifty specific camels, that is permissible. This is if the settlement is for more than the type that was ruled. As for if the settlement is for less than what was ruled, it is permissible immediately or deferred. If they settle on a different type from what was ruled, and he settled for more than what was ruled, it is permissible. What we have mentioned is if they settle after the ruling or consent. As for if they settle before the ruling, if the settled amount is more than the diya, it is not permissible. Ibn Sama'a from Muhammad: if two men wounded a man intentionally, and qisas was decreed against one, then he died from the two wounds, he said: his heirs may kill the other.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage brings together multiple fatwas from Hanafi masters. First, from Abu Yusuf: if a wounder settles for an accidental wound, then the victim dies, the settlement is partially void (only one-third deducted from 'aqila, per Sahibayn). According to Abu Hanifa, the settlement does not cover future death, so if death occurs, the settlement is void entirely, and the full diya is on the 'aqila. Then from al-Zahiriyya: if a settlement exceeds the qadi's ruling, its validity depends on timing and type. If after ruling, settlement for more than the diya is void; if for less, it is valid. If the type differs, increase may be allowed in certain conditions (e.g., specific camels hand-to-hand). Before ruling, settlement for more than diya is void. Finally, from Ibn Sama'a from Muhammad: if two men intentionally wound, and qisas is decreed against one, but the victim dies from both wounds, the heirs may kill the other (the one not decreed against). This shows that death from combined wounds can still trigger qisas against the second.

Key Terms
الموضحة (al-mudiha): A head wound that exposes the bone.
يحط عن العاقلة الثلث (yuhittu 'an al-'aqila al-thuluth): One-third is deducted from the 'aqila's liability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi view in the Hanafi school, if a wounder settles for an accidental mudiha wound and the victim later dies, what happens to the 'aqila's liability?
A) They pay full diya.
B) They pay two-thirds diya.
C) They pay nothing.
D) They pay half diya.

Key Takeaway
A settlement for an accidental wound does not automatically cover subsequent death; according to the mufta bihi view, the 'aqila pays two-thirds diya and the wounder recovers his payment.
